<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c157a993342c4ef7806938e2c964fb53"><span data-offset-key="c157a993342c4ef7806938e2c964fb53:0">Logging to a File</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fa74722131574ed3897d805111b4d420"><span data-offset-key="fa74722131574ed3897d805111b4d420:0">Instead of displaying the log messages to the screen, you can write them to a text file. The logging.basicConfig() function takes a filename keyword argument, like so:</span></span></span>

    import logging​logging.basicConfig(filename='myProgramLog.txt', level=logging.DEBUG, format='%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s')

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="87ebf60e07b34f39a7a6c0f939879c85"><span data-offset-key="87ebf60e07b34f39a7a6c0f939879c85:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://github.com/Web-Dev-Collaborative/python-cheatsheet#python-cheatsheet" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="2903b2065edd434fb949acb2009cc757"><span data-offset-key="2903b2065edd434fb949acb2009cc757:0"><em>Return to the Top</em></span></span></a><span data-key="b82be08fd7df408382ecf18fe3ff49c3"><span data-offset-key="b82be08fd7df408382ecf18fe3ff49c3:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1d4bc214670a47ce90fc437eff93586e"><span data-offset-key="1d4bc214670a47ce90fc437eff93586e:0">Lambda Functions</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e7af1074b60748839677653c43609bdb"><span data-offset-key="e7af1074b60748839677653c43609bdb:0">This function:</span></span></span>

    >>> def add(x, y):        return x + y​>>> add(5, 3)8

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="33bb9c1272a34133baf3ad823854cd19"><span data-offset-key="33bb9c1272a34133baf3ad823854cd19:0">Is equivalent to the </span><span data-offset-key="33bb9c1272a34133baf3ad823854cd19:1">*lambda*</span><span data-offset-key="33bb9c1272a34133baf3ad823854cd19:2"> function:</span></span></span>

    >>> add = lambda x, y: x + y>>> add(5, 3)8

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="59ae8ae4d42643c9a8c1e9db3257696c"><span data-offset-key="59ae8ae4d42643c9a8c1e9db3257696c:0">It's not even need to bind it to a name like add before:</span></span></span>

    >>> (lambda x, y: x + y)(5, 3)8

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cc3af7de8bd642c9b4775af6813a89fe"><span data-offset-key="cc3af7de8bd642c9b4775af6813a89fe:0">Like regular nested functions, lambdas also work as lexical closures:</span></span></span>

    >>> def make_adder(n):        return lambda x: x + n​>>> plus_3 = make_adder(3)>>> plus_5 = make_adder(5)​>>> plus_3(4)7>>> plus_5(4)9

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d27dc510c5a444fb8588373a3202cd97"><span data-offset-key="d27dc510c5a444fb8588373a3202cd97:0">Note: lambda can only evaluate an expression, like a single line of code.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8a8fa2da469a4069a012151f28acf1cb"><span data-offset-key="8a8fa2da469a4069a012151f28acf1cb:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://github.com/Web-Dev-Collaborative/python-cheatsheet#python-cheatsheet" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="1920fed42fd74ee98f32b83860897ebc"><span data-offset-key="1920fed42fd74ee98f32b83860897ebc:0"><em>Return to the Top</em></span></span></a><span data-key="4194593eff7c4a348b897aceef95bdfa"><span data-offset-key="4194593eff7c4a348b897aceef95bdfa:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="349aa28c52454ae5b3d7fb7a55b9797e"><span data-offset-key="349aa28c52454ae5b3d7fb7a55b9797e:0">Ternary Conditional Operator</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="939cac219e104d9d915ad5f64e062617"><span data-offset-key="939cac219e104d9d915ad5f64e062617:0">Many programming languages have a ternary operator, which define a conditional expression. The most common usage is to make a terse simple conditional assignment statement. In other words, it offers one-line code to evaluate the first expression if the condition is true, otherwise it evaluates the second expression.</span></span></span>

    <expression1> if <condition> else <expression2>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="50e3dba203b84209bffa0af8689f3925"><span data-offset-key="50e3dba203b84209bffa0af8689f3925:0">Example:</span></span></span>

    >>> age = 15​>>> print('kid' if age < 18 else 'adult')kid

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4cdb4fa0c8d94d2ca34e9426b0383be3"><span data-offset-key="4cdb4fa0c8d94d2ca34e9426b0383be3:0">Ternary operators can be chained:</span></span></span>

    >>> age = 15​>>> print('kid' if age < 13 else 'teenager' if age < 18 else 'adult')teenager

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7555ec3bcd8b4afcad2e45773f70b110"><span data-offset-key="7555ec3bcd8b4afcad2e45773f70b110:0">The code above is equivalent to:</span></span></span>

    if age < 18:    if age < 13:        print('kid')    else:        print('teenager')else:    print('adult')

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="daca1399106a45b3943541e8bd764d59"><span data-offset-key="daca1399106a45b3943541e8bd764d59:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://github.com/Web-Dev-Collaborative/python-cheatsheet#python-cheatsheet" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4679efa06c724a94a067a9b7eb888bc8"><span data-offset-key="4679efa06c724a94a067a9b7eb888bc8:0"><em>Return to the Top</em></span></span></a><span data-key="ccef843caf1544718f2dc69f1758ef21"><span data-offset-key="ccef843caf1544718f2dc69f1758ef21:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fcfdd4829120432e83b01501865cf06b"><span data-offset-key="fcfdd4829120432e83b01501865cf06b:0">args and kwargs</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="930e23589ef84e13be9f105d366034df"><span data-offset-key="930e23589ef84e13be9f105d366034df:0">The names </span><span data-offset-key="930e23589ef84e13be9f105d366034df:1">`args and kwargs`</span><span data-offset-key="930e23589ef84e13be9f105d366034df:2"> are arbitrary - the important thing are the </span><span data-offset-key="930e23589ef84e13be9f105d366034df:3">`*`</span><span data-offset-key="930e23589ef84e13be9f105d366034df:4"> and </span><span data-offset-key="930e23589ef84e13be9f105d366034df:5">`**`</span><span data-offset-key="930e23589ef84e13be9f105d366034df:6"> operators. They can mean:</span></span></span>

1.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="330d4fcb626b4c0c9d6aadd2eab39dc9"><span data-offset-key="330d4fcb626b4c0c9d6aadd2eab39dc9:0">In a function declaration, </span><span data-offset-key="330d4fcb626b4c0c9d6aadd2eab39dc9:1">`*`</span><span data-offset-key="330d4fcb626b4c0c9d6aadd2eab39dc9:2"> means “pack all remaining positional arguments into a tuple named </span><span data-offset-key="330d4fcb626b4c0c9d6aadd2eab39dc9:3">`<name>`</span><span data-offset-key="330d4fcb626b4c0c9d6aadd2eab39dc9:4">”, while </span><span data-offset-key="330d4fcb626b4c0c9d6aadd2eab39dc9:5">`**`</span><span data-offset-key="330d4fcb626b4c0c9d6aadd2eab39dc9:6"> is the same for keyword arguments (except it uses a dictionary, not a tuple).</span></span></span>

2.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="bbfd5d36042b459c9e530a7bb90ce502"><span data-offset-key="bbfd5d36042b459c9e530a7bb90ce502:0">In a function call, </span><span data-offset-key="bbfd5d36042b459c9e530a7bb90ce502:1">`*`</span><span data-offset-key="bbfd5d36042b459c9e530a7bb90ce502:2"> means “unpack tuple or list named </span><span data-offset-key="bbfd5d36042b459c9e530a7bb90ce502:3">`<name>`</span><span data-offset-key="bbfd5d36042b459c9e530a7bb90ce502:4"> to positional arguments at this position”, while </span><span data-offset-key="bbfd5d36042b459c9e530a7bb90ce502:5">`**`</span><span data-offset-key="bbfd5d36042b459c9e530a7bb90ce502:6"> is the same for keyword arguments.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a28e8ccc0501471893e30f063a888423"><span data-offset-key="a28e8ccc0501471893e30f063a888423:0">For example you can make a function that you can use to call any other function, no matter what parameters it has:</span></span></span>

    def forward(f, *args, **kwargs):    return f(*args, **kwargs)

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2da3c034ddcc42f39aba5a7c13299d7a"><span data-offset-key="2da3c034ddcc42f39aba5a7c13299d7a:0">Inside forward, args is a tuple (of all positional arguments except the first one, because we specified it - the f), kwargs is a dict. Then we call f and unpack them so they become normal arguments to f.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ca05e04122e642c0a6db09ceabb1da8e"><span data-offset-key="ca05e04122e642c0a6db09ceabb1da8e:0">You use </span><span data-offset-key="ca05e04122e642c0a6db09ceabb1da8e:1">`*args`</span><span data-offset-key="ca05e04122e642c0a6db09ceabb1da8e:2"> when you have an indefinite amount of positional arguments.</span></span></span>

    >>> def fruits(*args):>>>    for fruit in args:>>>       print(fruit)​>>> fruits("apples", "bananas", "grapes")​"apples""bananas""grapes"

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a12810589d8642fea4f114d1ae179e94"><span data-offset-key="a12810589d8642fea4f114d1ae179e94:0">Similarly, you use </span><span data-offset-key="a12810589d8642fea4f114d1ae179e94:1">`**kwargs`</span><span data-offset-key="a12810589d8642fea4f114d1ae179e94:2"> when you have an indefinite number of keyword arguments.</span></span></span>

    >>> def fruit(**kwargs):>>>    for key, value in kwargs.items():>>>        print("{0}: {1}".format(key, value))​>>> fruit(name = "apple", color = "red")​name: applecolor: red

    >>> def show(arg1, arg2, *args, kwarg1=None, kwarg2=None, **kwargs):>>>   print(arg1)>>>   print(arg2)>>>   print(args)>>>   print(kwarg1)>>>   print(kwarg2)>>>   print(kwargs)​>>> data1 = [1,2,3]>>> data2 = [4,5,6]>>> data3 = {'a':7,'b':8,'c':9}​>>> show(*data1,*data2, kwarg1="python",kwarg2="cheatsheet",**data3)12(3, 4, 5, 6)pythoncheatsheet{'a': 7, 'b': 8, 'c': 9}​>>> show(*data1, *data2, **data3)12(3, 4, 5, 6)NoneNone{'a': 7, 'b': 8, 'c': 9}​# If you do not specify ** for kwargs>>> show(*data1, *data2, *data3)12(3, 4, 5, 6, "a", "b", "c")NoneNone{}

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="67ef84bfdf91453c90e4ed3d7512e083"><span data-offset-key="67ef84bfdf91453c90e4ed3d7512e083:0">Things to Remember(args)</span></span></span>

1.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d49c63ad1a8f4a46b331bb5d86e68db9"><span data-offset-key="d49c63ad1a8f4a46b331bb5d86e68db9:0">Functions can accept a variable number of positional arguments by using </span><span data-offset-key="d49c63ad1a8f4a46b331bb5d86e68db9:1">`*args`</span><span data-offset-key="d49c63ad1a8f4a46b331bb5d86e68db9:2"> in the def statement.</span></span></span>

2.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6b860206d252471b8515be104401acc6"><span data-offset-key="6b860206d252471b8515be104401acc6:0">You can use the items from a sequence as the positional arguments for a function with the </span><span data-offset-key="6b860206d252471b8515be104401acc6:1">`*`</span><span data-offset-key="6b860206d252471b8515be104401acc6:2"> operator.</span></span></span>

3.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="84de221751f34c26b2e78d16d1c0fc9c"><span data-offset-key="84de221751f34c26b2e78d16d1c0fc9c:0">Using the </span><span data-offset-key="84de221751f34c26b2e78d16d1c0fc9c:1">`*`</span><span data-offset-key="84de221751f34c26b2e78d16d1c0fc9c:2"> operator with a generator may cause your program to run out of memory and crash.</span></span></span>

4.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e9f6071af0cb43de92aaabf312fb048e"><span data-offset-key="e9f6071af0cb43de92aaabf312fb048e:0">Adding new positional parameters to functions that accept </span><span data-offset-key="e9f6071af0cb43de92aaabf312fb048e:1">`*args`</span><span data-offset-key="e9f6071af0cb43de92aaabf312fb048e:2"> can introduce hard-to-find bugs.</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1d3de4e293c34120b11f49b5bffe43e2"><span data-offset-key="1d3de4e293c34120b11f49b5bffe43e2:0">Things to Remember(kwargs)</span></span></span>

1.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2b7ef027e06245d494b32fe6747a44c9"><span data-offset-key="2b7ef027e06245d494b32fe6747a44c9:0">Function arguments can be specified by position or by keyword.</span></span></span>

2.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c02588f3781a4a4f9338fb19637636b3"><span data-offset-key="c02588f3781a4a4f9338fb19637636b3:0">Keywords make it clear what the purpose of each argument is when it would be confusing with only positional arguments.</span></span></span>

3.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c4374f8dc6b44eb3b839ee761a522f6f"><span data-offset-key="c4374f8dc6b44eb3b839ee761a522f6f:0">Keyword arguments with default values make it easy to add new behaviors to a function, especially when the function has existing callers.</span></span></span>

4.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e136fc2a252d4fd384ea31090a8adf7f"><span data-offset-key="e136fc2a252d4fd384ea31090a8adf7f:0">Optional keyword arguments should always be passed by keyword instead of by position.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4613b0cfcd10488095b5b2cfba41fa7e"><span data-offset-key="4613b0cfcd10488095b5b2cfba41fa7e:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://github.com/Web-Dev-Collaborative/python-cheatsheet#python-cheatsheet" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="2b9c8e549b2441d6890c00fcafa421a0"><span data-offset-key="2b9c8e549b2441d6890c00fcafa421a0:0"><em>Return to the Top</em></span></span></a><span data-key="a1e5768e50f24f06b0ee45898e3843db"><span data-offset-key="a1e5768e50f24f06b0ee45898e3843db:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="74c65993cdbb4d1dbe40bf01ef8eda13"><span data-offset-key="74c65993cdbb4d1dbe40bf01ef8eda13:0">Context Manager</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="06c3c66b962c42a590d6309b55d93c28"><span data-offset-key="06c3c66b962c42a590d6309b55d93c28:0">While Python's context managers are widely used, few understand the purpose behind their use. These statements, commonly used with reading and writing files, assist the application in conserving system memory and improve resource management by ensuring specific resources are only in use for certain processes.</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3367f4820677438ea3f970f4013c65ac"><span data-offset-key="3367f4820677438ea3f970f4013c65ac:0">with statement</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2139872406e54b518a85f3c1b4d1a4c1"><span data-offset-key="2139872406e54b518a85f3c1b4d1a4c1:0">A context manager is an object that is notified when a context (a block of code) starts and ends. You commonly use one with the with statement. It takes care of the notifying.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0f1c2c3ba6704ebaa3d06b26b711ef9e"><span data-offset-key="0f1c2c3ba6704ebaa3d06b26b711ef9e:0">For example, file objects are context managers. When a context ends, the file object is closed automatically:</span></span></span>

    >>> with open(filename) as f:>>>     file_contents = f.read()​# the open_file object has automatically been closed.

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1359b619fbc0497f899a40ff41c3b6d7"><span data-offset-key="1359b619fbc0497f899a40ff41c3b6d7:0">Anything that ends execution of the block causes the context manager's exit method to be called. This includes exceptions, and can be useful when an error causes you to prematurely exit from an open file or connection. Exiting a script without properly closing files/connections is a bad idea, that may cause data loss or other problems. By using a context manager you can ensure that precautions are always taken to prevent damage or loss in this way.</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d7c0ed0f67c4451791743c629618c009"><span data-offset-key="d7c0ed0f67c4451791743c629618c009:0">Writing your own contextmanager using generator syntax</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5864511b3f8b4071b112c0c056ea3554"><span data-offset-key="5864511b3f8b4071b112c0c056ea3554:0">It is also possible to write a context manager using generator syntax thanks to the </span><span data-offset-key="5864511b3f8b4071b112c0c056ea3554:1">`contextlib.contextmanager`</span><span data-offset-key="5864511b3f8b4071b112c0c056ea3554:2"> decorator:</span></span></span>

    >>> import contextlib>>> @contextlib.contextmanager... def context_manager(num):...     print('Enter')...     yield num + 1...     print('Exit')>>> with context_manager(2) as cm:...     # the following instructions are run when the 'yield' point of the context...     # manager is reached....     # 'cm' will have the value that was yielded...     print('Right in the middle with cm = {}'.format(cm))EnterRight in the middle with cm = 3Exit​>>>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5a9be0922cf94922973c5a27eeba5772"><span data-offset-key="5a9be0922cf94922973c5a27eeba5772:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://github.com/Web-Dev-Collaborative/python-cheatsheet#python-cheatsheet" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="88e8cb92ccb54f9389dc3099ef4c93b3"><span data-offset-key="88e8cb92ccb54f9389dc3099ef4c93b3:0"><em>Return to the Top</em></span></span></a><span data-key="39d3e86377e742c596af0f528356f5e8"><span data-offset-key="39d3e86377e742c596af0f528356f5e8:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="412e1378f6e4428dbba9a6cce89fd743"><span data-offset-key="412e1378f6e4428dbba9a6cce89fd743:0">`__main__`</span><span data-offset-key="412e1378f6e4428dbba9a6cce89fd743:1"> Top-level script environment</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="bb98d9d103974bf7829469d6589f160f"><span data-offset-key="bb98d9d103974bf7829469d6589f160f:0">`__main__`</span><span data-offset-key="bb98d9d103974bf7829469d6589f160f:1"> is the name of the scope in which top-level code executes. A module’s </span><span data-offset-key="bb98d9d103974bf7829469d6589f160f:2">**name**</span><span data-offset-key="bb98d9d103974bf7829469d6589f160f:3"> is set equal to </span><span data-offset-key="bb98d9d103974bf7829469d6589f160f:4">`__main__`</span><span data-offset-key="bb98d9d103974bf7829469d6589f160f:5"> when read from standard input, a script, or from an interactive prompt.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="304851e94c8d4b9681a5d60fddca16dd"><span data-offset-key="304851e94c8d4b9681a5d60fddca16dd:0">A module can discover whether or not it is running in the main scope by checking its own </span><span data-offset-key="304851e94c8d4b9681a5d60fddca16dd:1">`__name__`</span><span data-offset-key="304851e94c8d4b9681a5d60fddca16dd:2">, which allows a common idiom for conditionally executing code in a module when it is run as a script or with </span><span data-offset-key="304851e94c8d4b9681a5d60fddca16dd:3">`python -m`</span><span data-offset-key="304851e94c8d4b9681a5d60fddca16dd:4"> but not when it is imported:</span></span></span>

    >>> if __name__ == "__main__":...     # execute only if run as a script...     main()

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="663dc89f20624affa884b6daf0d75edf"><span data-offset-key="663dc89f20624affa884b6daf0d75edf:0">For a package, the same effect can be achieved by including a </span><span data-offset-key="663dc89f20624affa884b6daf0d75edf:1">**main**</span><span data-offset-key="663dc89f20624affa884b6daf0d75edf:2">.py module, the contents of which will be executed when the module is run with -m</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e20380d807eb46da9ce7a56627c05c7d"><span data-offset-key="e20380d807eb46da9ce7a56627c05c7d:0">For example we are developing script which is designed to be used as module, we should do:</span></span></span>

    >>> # Python program to execute function directly>>> def add(a, b):...     return a+b...>>> add(10, 20) # we can test it by calling the function save it as calculate.py30>>> # Now if we want to use that module by importing we have to comment out our call,>>> # Instead we can write like this in calculate.py>>> if __name__ == "__main__":...     add(3, 5)...>>> import calculate>>> calculate.add(3, 5)8

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fb238cb3c53d4214958d38921efad0c1"><span data-offset-key="fb238cb3c53d4214958d38921efad0c1:0">Advantages</span></span></span>

1.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="45175197afbe42a4981415366dbb65de"><span data-offset-key="45175197afbe42a4981415366dbb65de:0">Every Python module has it’s </span><span data-offset-key="45175197afbe42a4981415366dbb65de:1">`__name__`</span><span data-offset-key="45175197afbe42a4981415366dbb65de:2"> defined and if this is </span><span data-offset-key="45175197afbe42a4981415366dbb65de:3">`__main__`</span><span data-offset-key="45175197afbe42a4981415366dbb65de:4">, it implies that the module is being run standalone by the user and we can do corresponding appropriate actions.</span></span></span>

2.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f16531673ff043a28f1ab37ae6ac2fae"><span data-offset-key="f16531673ff043a28f1ab37ae6ac2fae:0">If you import this script as a module in another script, the </span><span data-offset-key="f16531673ff043a28f1ab37ae6ac2fae:1">**name**</span><span data-offset-key="f16531673ff043a28f1ab37ae6ac2fae:2"> is set to the name of the script/module.</span></span></span>

3.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c7291ee234d841b3945b4fa0f7ab477a"><span data-offset-key="c7291ee234d841b3945b4fa0f7ab477a:0">Python files can act as either reusable modules, or as standalone programs.</span></span></span>

4.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e6dc9199196f4a8189accf98c0f94d02"><span data-offset-key="e6dc9199196f4a8189accf98c0f94d02:0">if </span><span data-offset-key="e6dc9199196f4a8189accf98c0f94d02:1">`__name__ == “main”:`</span><span data-offset-key="e6dc9199196f4a8189accf98c0f94d02:2"> is used to execute some code only if the file was run directly, and not imported.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0f339fa7eb4f4cca936e3e7fb6e3da1f"><span data-offset-key="0f339fa7eb4f4cca936e3e7fb6e3da1f:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://github.com/Web-Dev-Collaborative/python-cheatsheet#python-cheatsheet" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="30616088491642edbe8146d7bd96bfe0"><span data-offset-key="30616088491642edbe8146d7bd96bfe0:0"><em>Return to the Top</em></span></span></a><span data-key="7781ad65da5a45149bf02d3f16c42245"><span data-offset-key="7781ad65da5a45149bf02d3f16c42245:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ab4fa43ccd8d4b3b9bfed70d235e5fdf"><span data-offset-key="ab4fa43ccd8d4b3b9bfed70d235e5fdf:0">setup.py</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d83a4baa38ed410ca0dff05e65fe3bf6"><span data-offset-key="d83a4baa38ed410ca0dff05e65fe3bf6:0">The setup script is the centre of all activity in building, distributing, and installing modules using the Distutils. The main purpose of the setup script is to describe your module distribution to the Distutils, so that the various commands that operate on your modules do the right thing.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e3450750f5a044baa0d8826f05116f80"><span data-offset-key="e3450750f5a044baa0d8826f05116f80:0">The </span><span data-offset-key="e3450750f5a044baa0d8826f05116f80:1">`setup.py`</span><span data-offset-key="e3450750f5a044baa0d8826f05116f80:2"> file is at the heart of a Python project. It describes all of the metadata about your project. There a quite a few fields you can add to a project to give it a rich set of metadata describing the project. However, there are only three required fields: name, version, and packages. The name field must be unique if you wish to publish your package on the Python Package Index (PyPI). The version field keeps track of different releases of the project. The packages field describes where you’ve put the Python source code within your project.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="00ce3091eade4499bc7073180142d4e8"><span data-offset-key="00ce3091eade4499bc7073180142d4e8:0">This allows you to easily install Python packages. Often it's enough to write:</span></span></span>

    python setup.py install

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6cd664bc7f4544e09b9c47485243b08b"><span data-offset-key="6cd664bc7f4544e09b9c47485243b08b:0">and module will install itself.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="19d87c09a0cd4f53b09627249efee7bc"><span data-offset-key="19d87c09a0cd4f53b09627249efee7bc:0">Our initial setup.py will also include information about the license and will re-use the README.txt file for the long\_description field. This will look like:</span></span></span>

    >>> from distutils.core import setup>>> setup(...    name='pythonCheatsheet',...    version='0.1',...    packages=['pipenv',],...    license='MIT',...    long_description=open('README.txt').read(),... )

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="16d59e82015746589b835e1c33a4ac37"><span data-offset-key="16d59e82015746589b835e1c33a4ac37:0">Find more information visit </span></span><a href="http://docs.python.org/install/index.html" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="a6150cd2c42f424dbc81e4f2af8c8e5e"><span data-offset-key="a6150cd2c42f424dbc81e4f2af8c8e5e:0">http://docs.python.org/install/index.html</span></span></a><span data-key="4c8252f9c84e46fabd3cfdcd125400e5"><span data-offset-key="4c8252f9c84e46fabd3cfdcd125400e5:0">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9aa2d8a23b3645619bc79bb5597444be"><span data-offset-key="9aa2d8a23b3645619bc79bb5597444be:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://github.com/Web-Dev-Collaborative/python-cheatsheet#python-cheatsheet" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="a1721a4a458d4dc0b438252171bd9387"><span data-offset-key="a1721a4a458d4dc0b438252171bd9387:0"><em>Return to the Top</em></span></span></a><span data-key="9f9c6fc35ec24ce1ba8d8ff7d8882a0c"><span data-offset-key="9f9c6fc35ec24ce1ba8d8ff7d8882a0c:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f7b9cf9c5a7a48f2b8e9ea136e29c803"><span data-offset-key="f7b9cf9c5a7a48f2b8e9ea136e29c803:0">Dataclasses</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="83b8452243c74924ba8fceb85c7231b1"><span data-offset-key="83b8452243c74924ba8fceb85c7231b1:0">`Dataclasses`</span><span data-offset-key="83b8452243c74924ba8fceb85c7231b1:1"> are python classes but are suited for storing data objects. This module provides a decorator and functions for automatically adding generated special methods such as </span><span data-offset-key="83b8452243c74924ba8fceb85c7231b1:2">`__init__()`</span><span data-offset-key="83b8452243c74924ba8fceb85c7231b1:3"> and </span><span data-offset-key="83b8452243c74924ba8fceb85c7231b1:4">`__repr__()`</span><span data-offset-key="83b8452243c74924ba8fceb85c7231b1:5"> to user-defined classes.</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="336d79d6d36b4039ae69b734153bbf73"><span data-offset-key="336d79d6d36b4039ae69b734153bbf73:0">Features</span></span></span>

1.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4971371a247244e9934b80a070e18492"><span data-offset-key="4971371a247244e9934b80a070e18492:0">They store data and represent a certain data type. Ex: A number. For people familiar with ORMs, a model instance is a data object. It represents a specific kind of entity. It holds attributes that define or represent the entity.</span></span></span>

2.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="792b43c7344a45ce9d7c001cf57fd4e5"><span data-offset-key="792b43c7344a45ce9d7c001cf57fd4e5:0">They can be compared to other objects of the same type. Ex: A number can be greater than, less than, or equal to another number.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="abaff4e934d448da8025fd8dc010ed5f"><span data-offset-key="abaff4e934d448da8025fd8dc010ed5f:0">Python 3.7 provides a decorator dataclass that is used to convert a class into a dataclass.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4d7aebe2a3bc4d1d96a977e7797894c8"><span data-offset-key="4d7aebe2a3bc4d1d96a977e7797894c8:0">python 2.7</span></span></span>

    >>> class Number:...     def __init__(self, val):...         self.val = val...>>> obj = Number(2)>>> obj.val2

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="29a3994045bb4cae9b57d07de5d12f37"><span data-offset-key="29a3994045bb4cae9b57d07de5d12f37:0">with dataclass</span></span></span>

    >>> @dataclass... class Number:...     val: int...>>> obj = Number(2)>>> obj.val2

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b34364d9e26541b58e553e06db7e70fb"><span data-offset-key="b34364d9e26541b58e553e06db7e70fb:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://github.com/Web-Dev-Collaborative/python-cheatsheet#python-cheatsheet" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="0395fe26e1dc4914be01442fb55e9fb3"><span data-offset-key="0395fe26e1dc4914be01442fb55e9fb3:0"><em>Return to the Top</em></span></span></a><span data-key="8e92193b74584b1ebabef7152ad0baad"><span data-offset-key="8e92193b74584b1ebabef7152ad0baad:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="02170c50323545ad85911c8c34718989"><span data-offset-key="02170c50323545ad85911c8c34718989:0">Default values</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="966dddd6b7234d4cab5e18d1e72bbab9"><span data-offset-key="966dddd6b7234d4cab5e18d1e72bbab9:0">It is easy to add default values to the fields of your data class.</span></span></span>

    >>> @dataclass... class Product:...     name: str...     count: int = 0...     price: float = 0.0...>>> obj = Product("Python")>>> obj.namePython>>> obj.count0>>> obj.price0.0

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f27f771da7cb48a889cd658d4d037005"><span data-offset-key="f27f771da7cb48a889cd658d4d037005:0">Type hints</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a79da8a5fa2f41b19ec73896cefbc10e"><span data-offset-key="a79da8a5fa2f41b19ec73896cefbc10e:0">It is mandatory to define the data type in dataclass. However, If you don't want specify the datatype then, use </span><span data-offset-key="a79da8a5fa2f41b19ec73896cefbc10e:1">`typing.Any`</span><span data-offset-key="a79da8a5fa2f41b19ec73896cefbc10e:2">.</span></span></span>

    >>> from dataclasses import dataclass>>> from typing import Any​>>> @dataclass... class WithoutExplicitTypes:...    name: Any...    value: Any = 42...

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="31019d97e6fb4f0a86cf71b3e32c10b9"><span data-offset-key="31019d97e6fb4f0a86cf71b3e32c10b9:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://github.com/Web-Dev-Collaborative/python-cheatsheet#python-cheatsheet" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="21ce81a45f7144839d17337360c6f294"><span data-offset-key="21ce81a45f7144839d17337360c6f294:0"><em>Return to the Top</em></span></span></a><span data-key="15d9a0ca46c945759560d00c4f3882cb"><span data-offset-key="15d9a0ca46c945759560d00c4f3882cb:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="12f3ab5a74ba4d418cf8789918d2c534"><span data-offset-key="12f3ab5a74ba4d418cf8789918d2c534:0">Virtual Environment</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fbc0e4f57d124a478a4be114aacdb704"><span data-offset-key="fbc0e4f57d124a478a4be114aacdb704:0">The use of a Virtual Environment is to test python code in encapsulated environments and to also avoid filling the base Python installation with libraries we might use for only one project.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1a6623baccd84048a4e80e4e08d8e111"><span data-offset-key="1a6623baccd84048a4e80e4e08d8e111:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://github.com/Web-Dev-Collaborative/python-cheatsheet#python-cheatsheet" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="fd0c833793e141e68e7ae180aaed7aa2"><span data-offset-key="fd0c833793e141e68e7ae180aaed7aa2:0"><em>Return to the Top</em></span></span></a><span data-key="2ea39e6eb91441518a5d4457777295a5"><span data-offset-key="2ea39e6eb91441518a5d4457777295a5:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="bf00a74c8ff24f628435f46a6fc773ad"><span data-offset-key="bf00a74c8ff24f628435f46a6fc773ad:0">virtualenv</span></span></span>

1.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ddc53efe8f8b441fbec605b2dbfad2e0"><span data-offset-key="ddc53efe8f8b441fbec605b2dbfad2e0:0">Install virtualenv</span></span></span>

        pip install virtualenv

2.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7ab9e894aa5f482b8b5077c74acf07df"><span data-offset-key="7ab9e894aa5f482b8b5077c74acf07df:0">Install virtualenvwrapper-win (Windows)</span></span></span>

        pip install virtualenvwrapper-win

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="60995db5caf24891a628864725ce5061"><span data-offset-key="60995db5caf24891a628864725ce5061:0">Usage:</span></span></span>

1.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="531f4b9b8c9341d1a18a3017c7101c0c"><span data-offset-key="531f4b9b8c9341d1a18a3017c7101c0c:0">Make a Virtual Environment</span></span></span>

        mkvirtualenv HelloWold

    <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b9a073e4eb204e9f9d51b938aa768bde"><span data-offset-key="b9a073e4eb204e9f9d51b938aa768bde:0">Anything we install now will be specific to this project. And available to the projects we connect to this environment.</span></span></span>

2.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7322311e660947c99cfcd67859a7d3e3"><span data-offset-key="7322311e660947c99cfcd67859a7d3e3:0">Set Project Directory</span></span></span>

    <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3aa7bb06b4d64580b3335f525a28d26e"><span data-offset-key="3aa7bb06b4d64580b3335f525a28d26e:0">To bind our virtualenv with our current working directory we simply enter:</span></span></span>

        setprojectdir .

3.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f9650612619e409c99e2c1099e575c5a"><span data-offset-key="f9650612619e409c99e2c1099e575c5a:0">Deactivate</span></span></span>

    <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2db9e2413f154a09b05d473e456f16e0"><span data-offset-key="2db9e2413f154a09b05d473e456f16e0:0">To move onto something else in the command line type ‘deactivate’ to deactivate your environment.</span></span></span>

        deactivate

    <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d7a2abe631384179911e446be193be96"><span data-offset-key="d7a2abe631384179911e446be193be96:0">Notice how the parenthesis disappear.</span></span></span>

4.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7a376c2d72b94ec088a22efdab77c0bb"><span data-offset-key="7a376c2d72b94ec088a22efdab77c0bb:0">Workon</span></span></span>

    <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f0246a9545fc4bed8c8da2f5e0a7b47e"><span data-offset-key="f0246a9545fc4bed8c8da2f5e0a7b47e:0">Open up the command prompt and type ‘workon HelloWold’ to activate the environment and move into your root project folder</span></span></span>

        workon HelloWold

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0654a89f2f254eac9ee1e495fc9f3aa9"><span data-offset-key="0654a89f2f254eac9ee1e495fc9f3aa9:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://github.com/Web-Dev-Collaborative/python-cheatsheet#python-cheatsheet" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="700a2698d84e4eb6991af40c1354cc57"><span data-offset-key="700a2698d84e4eb6991af40c1354cc57:0"><em>Return to the Top</em></span></span></a><span data-key="92abec2484864d019adfc4f45f541245"><span data-offset-key="92abec2484864d019adfc4f45f541245:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="038430ac9a2a4208b7959707cfec7e25"><span data-offset-key="038430ac9a2a4208b7959707cfec7e25:0">poetry</span></span></span>

> <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0c14e62c691c41059dbd6249b8a4c132"><span data-offset-key="0c14e62c691c41059dbd6249b8a4c132:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://poetry.eustace.io/" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="d0ecca9f154e4f7ea16ed538bbf6d289"><span data-offset-key="d0ecca9f154e4f7ea16ed538bbf6d289:0">Poetry</span></span></a><span data-key="d5494c518ebd44d8b2273e43f603a2e3"><span data-offset-key="d5494c518ebd44d8b2273e43f603a2e3:0"> is a tool for dependency management and packaging in Python. It allows you to declare the libraries your project depends on and it will manage (install/update) them for you.</span></span></span>

1.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ae8cfe60650c40e4a5a31ab0cdb2280a"><span data-offset-key="ae8cfe60650c40e4a5a31ab0cdb2280a:0">Install Poetry</span></span></span>

        pip install --user poetry

2.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="dc1e1d70d4ee48a39efb799aa4966dde"><span data-offset-key="dc1e1d70d4ee48a39efb799aa4966dde:0">Create a new project</span></span></span>

        poetry new my-project

    <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2280cb94b02d4cea832e0ada89c1a1d3"><span data-offset-key="2280cb94b02d4cea832e0ada89c1a1d3:0">This will create a my-project directory:</span></span></span>

        my-project├── pyproject.toml├── README.rst├── poetry_demo│   └── __init__.py└── tests    ├── __init__.py    └── test_poetry_demo.py

    <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="dae5eb723f844c9c832a9eb3665325e9"><span data-offset-key="dae5eb723f844c9c832a9eb3665325e9:0">The pyproject.toml file will orchestrate your project and its dependencies:</span></span></span>

        [tool.poetry]name = "my-project"version = "0.1.0"description = ""authors = ["your name <[email protected]>"]​[tool.poetry.dependencies]python = "*"​[tool.poetry.dev-dependencies]pytest = "^3.4"

3.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3214159a95c64782bc7b0825805941d9"><span data-offset-key="3214159a95c64782bc7b0825805941d9:0">Packages</span></span></span>

    <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="18dbea44a0f94ba3949160b172e7a376"><span data-offset-key="18dbea44a0f94ba3949160b172e7a376:0">To add dependencies to your project, you can specify them in the tool.poetry.dependencies section:</span></span></span>

        [tool.poetry.dependencies]pendulum = "^1.4"

    <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="be96f30f296042dc9cc0c9f4714b6994"><span data-offset-key="be96f30f296042dc9cc0c9f4714b6994:0">Also, instead of modifying the pyproject.toml file by hand, you can use the add command and it will automatically find a suitable version constraint.</span></span></span>

        $ poetry add pendulum

    <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f47b844a200f477b99b15172ca4534e3"><span data-offset-key="f47b844a200f477b99b15172ca4534e3:0">To install the dependencies listed in the pyproject.toml:</span></span></span>

        poetry install

    <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fcc548cf5cf146c68b32f4cd647b5511"><span data-offset-key="fcc548cf5cf146c68b32f4cd647b5511:0">To remove dependencies:</span></span></span>

        poetry remove pendulum

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d451ae7505964e069936d3ad13d0cda7"><span data-offset-key="d451ae7505964e069936d3ad13d0cda7:0">For more information, check the </span></span><a href="https://poetry.eustace.io/docs/" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="16ea08daacf3455aa4b287fdff8a09e6"><span data-offset-key="16ea08daacf3455aa4b287fdff8a09e6:0">documentation</span></span></a><span data-key="6eb88b31757d4cefaa88a8d5b7aeff63"><span data-offset-key="6eb88b31757d4cefaa88a8d5b7aeff63:0">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2f3285f6efca40059f7e8da494992b4d"><span data-offset-key="2f3285f6efca40059f7e8da494992b4d:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://github.com/Web-Dev-Collaborative/python-cheatsheet#python-cheatsheet" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="cbacb979da8f41c1a5e5d106cb60e067"><span data-offset-key="cbacb979da8f41c1a5e5d106cb60e067:0"><em>Return to the Top</em></span></span></a><span data-key="bc416bf07292408fad0e288b695d8245"><span data-offset-key="bc416bf07292408fad0e288b695d8245:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="35e9780df77a40cba23b1f2a749e468f"><span data-offset-key="35e9780df77a40cba23b1f2a749e468f:0">pipenv</span></span></span>

> <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0ebf943c288d42d491a033d1ecc0113a"><span data-offset-key="0ebf943c288d42d491a033d1ecc0113a:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://pipenv.readthedocs.io/en/latest/" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="f0957692e23747d6b2a38e9a5fa56c5f"><span data-offset-key="f0957692e23747d6b2a38e9a5fa56c5f:0">Pipenv</span></span></a><span data-key="c90a31722387472a87f922bbce863fed"><span data-offset-key="c90a31722387472a87f922bbce863fed:0"> is a tool that aims to bring the best of all packaging worlds (bundler, composer, npm, cargo, yarn, etc.) to the Python world. Windows is a first-class citizen, in our world.</span></span></span>

1.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fbd843ad828d41eebf7b2632f07ddbf9"><span data-offset-key="fbd843ad828d41eebf7b2632f07ddbf9:0">Install pipenv</span></span></span>

        pip install pipenv

2.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a91cec5997534eb1aaf92ceaf42317eb"><span data-offset-key="a91cec5997534eb1aaf92ceaf42317eb:0">Enter your Project directory and install the Packages for your project</span></span></span>

        cd my_projectpipenv install <package>

    <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="812e5a874d234c64a4f26c0757947226"><span data-offset-key="812e5a874d234c64a4f26c0757947226:0">Pipenv will install your package and create a Pipfile for you in your project’s directory. The Pipfile is used to track which dependencies your project needs in case you need to re-install them.</span></span></span>

3.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0624159854b646178e84799a2c57f0f6"><span data-offset-key="0624159854b646178e84799a2c57f0f6:0">Uninstall Packages</span></span></span>

        pipenv uninstall <package>

4.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="82b8f98984784b1db29cbd04c037928f"><span data-offset-key="82b8f98984784b1db29cbd04c037928f:0">Activate the Virtual Environment associated with your Python project</span></span></span>

        pipenv shell

5.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="92e055789de44c5099766d4da2a5517b"><span data-offset-key="92e055789de44c5099766d4da2a5517b:0">Exit the Virtual Environment</span></span></span>

        exit

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="176e67acbc614a549076cb1e37fe729e"><span data-offset-key="176e67acbc614a549076cb1e37fe729e:0">Find more information and a video in </span></span><a href="https://docs.pipenv.org/" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3cee979364484fdfbc84236cb2426517"><span data-offset-key="3cee979364484fdfbc84236cb2426517:0">docs.pipenv.org</span></span></a><span data-key="df72e06b6dac467eafbdbe8c72ef2430"><span data-offset-key="df72e06b6dac467eafbdbe8c72ef2430:0">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5c1797a358304f5aadc7431fab14e17e"><span data-offset-key="5c1797a358304f5aadc7431fab14e17e:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://github.com/Web-Dev-Collaborative/python-cheatsheet#python-cheatsheet" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="10808c0f1d624cf79dec5d1ff39c6ac5"><span data-offset-key="10808c0f1d624cf79dec5d1ff39c6ac5:0"><em>Return to the Top</em></span></span></a><span data-key="1f1d08c069e5476aa588c28fd10b126b"><span data-offset-key="1f1d08c069e5476aa588c28fd10b126b:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d13a2e8a4ad24391b211e3ae6aa0e57a"><span data-offset-key="d13a2e8a4ad24391b211e3ae6aa0e57a:0">anaconda</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d42a31ac8a3b49ec8dfb0f4c495290f7"><span data-offset-key="d42a31ac8a3b49ec8dfb0f4c495290f7:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://anaconda.org/" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="8bffb0b06dc24243a2de7932bb90fbc5"><span data-offset-key="8bffb0b06dc24243a2de7932bb90fbc5:0">Anaconda</span></span></a><span data-key="52af9d84323a4305baa436c554891ca8"><span data-offset-key="52af9d84323a4305baa436c554891ca8:0"> is another popular tool to manage python packages.</span></span></span>

> <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="27cf7883f61f42eba27b62a3e232b298"><span data-offset-key="27cf7883f61f42eba27b62a3e232b298:0">Where packages, notebooks, projects and environments are shared. Your place for free public conda package hosting.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a3cc833366af47ee980282c242137b3e"><span data-offset-key="a3cc833366af47ee980282c242137b3e:0">Usage:</span></span></span>

1.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1496e40a2d9345c3a96d7d845e81aa41"><span data-offset-key="1496e40a2d9345c3a96d7d845e81aa41:0">Make a Virtual Environment</span></span></span>

        conda create -n HelloWorld

2.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c64718c633484dca998e65ea04e60780"><span data-offset-key="c64718c633484dca998e65ea04e60780:0">To use the Virtual Environment, activate it by:</span></span></span>

        conda activate HelloWorld

    <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="709ac2c1a63442bd961eb0d4dab5eb2f"><span data-offset-key="709ac2c1a63442bd961eb0d4dab5eb2f:0">Anything installed now will be specific to the project HelloWorld</span></span></span>

3.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c1fd019774b34af4887dcdc69da886ed"><span data-offset-key="c1fd019774b34af4887dcdc69da886ed:0">Exit the Virtual Environment</span></span></span>

        conda deactivate

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">Flow Control</span></span>

<a href="python-cheat-sheet.html#Functions" class="reset-3c756112--menuItem-aa02f6ec--menuItemLight-757d5235--menuItemInline-173bdf97--pageTocItem-f4427024"></a>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">Functions</span></span>

<a href="python-cheat-sheet.html#Exception-Handling" class="reset-3c756112--menuItem-aa02f6ec--menuItemLight-757d5235--menuItemInline-173bdf97--pageTocItem-f4427024"></a>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">Exception Handling</span></span>

<a href="python-cheat-sheet.html#Lists" class="reset-3c756112--menuItem-aa02f6ec--menuItemLight-757d5235--menuItemInline-173bdf97--pageTocItem-f4427024"></a>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">Lists</span></span>

<a href="python-cheat-sheet.html#Dictionaries-and-Structuring-Data" class="reset-3c756112--menuItem-aa02f6ec--menuItemLight-757d5235--menuItemInline-173bdf97--pageTocItem-f4427024"></a>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">Dictionaries and Structuring Data</span></span>

<a href="python-cheat-sheet.html#sets" class="reset-3c756112--menuItem-aa02f6ec--menuItemLight-757d5235--menuItemInline-173bdf97--pageTocItem-f4427024"></a>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">sets</span></span>

<a href="python-cheat-sheet.html#itertools-Module" class="reset-3c756112--menuItem-aa02f6ec--menuItemLight-757d5235--menuItemInline-173bdf97--pageTocItem-f4427024"></a>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">itertools Module</span></span>

<a href="python-cheat-sheet.html#Comprehensions" class="reset-3c756112--menuItem-aa02f6ec--menuItemLight-757d5235--menuItemInline-173bdf97--pageTocItem-f4427024"></a>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">Comprehensions</span></span>

<a href="python-cheat-sheet.html#Manipulating-Strings" class="reset-3c756112--menuItem-aa02f6ec--menuItemLight-757d5235--menuItemInline-173bdf97--pageTocItem-f4427024"></a>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">Manipulating Strings</span></span>
